[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 're spending many cycles on guesses (all-keys-equal, altern
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ating patterns). Stop guessing key relationships — the task says 4 independent round ke
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ys each from a 20-bit seed. Use the structure you've already discovered: **
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] F is invertible**. That enables a clean meet-in-the-middle that needs no assumptions.

Key
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  plan (do this in C, it's fast):

1. Derive intermediate-
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] state equations precisely. With your notation, encryption is:
   - p
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] re: R ^= L
   - each round r: newR = L ^ F(R 
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ^ Kr); newL = R
   - post: L ^= R; output = merge(R_final, L_
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] final)

2. For a known (PT, CT), compute the **forward** state after 2 rounds as a function of (
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] K0,K1), and the **backward** state after 2 rounds as a function of (K2,K3). At the meeting point both must
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  equal the same 64-bit value (L2,R2).

3. Meet-in-the-middle: 
   - Loop K0 over 2^
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 20, K1 over 2^20 is 2^40 — too big directly. Instead exploit the Feistel half
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] -block structure so each side only depends on one key at the matching bo
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] undary. Specifically, after the pre-mix you know L0,R0 ex
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] actly. Round 0 output depends only on K0; round 1 output depends on K0 and K1. From
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  the cipher side, the post-mix is invertible so you know L
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 4,R4 exactly; the half-block that equals R
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] 3 = L4 is known, and L3 = R4 ^ F(L4 ^ K3) dep
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ends only on K3. So **K3 can be brute-forced to produce candidate (L3,R3)**, and **K0 can
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  be brute-forced to produce candidate (L1,R1)** independently. Then K1 (or K2) links them via one F evaluation that
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  you can solve/verify directly. That collapses 2^40 to roughly 2^20 +
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  2^20 work using a hash table on the meeting half-block.

   Concretely: For each K3 (2^20), compute R3=L4 
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] and store nothing yet (R3 is fixed, independent of K3 actually — note R3=L4 is
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  known with no key!). The unknown is L3 which depends on K3.
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  Meanwhile from plaintext side, after round 0, L1=R0, R1 = L0 ^ F(R0 ^ K0) depends
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  only on K0. Match the middle by noting R2 = L3 (known bo
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] undary) and L2 = R1... Trace the exact half-block that is key-independent at
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  the seam and use it as the hash key.

4. Practical robust fallback that's definitely correct and fast en
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ough: recover keys **one round at a time from the ciphertext side using multiple pairs**. For each gu
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ess of K3 (2^20), peel round 3 off ALL 32 ciphertexts to get cand
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] idate (L3,R3) for every pair. You can't validate K3 alone — but you CAN once
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  you also guess K2: peel round 2, then K1, then K0, checking against the known
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  plaintext. That's 2^80 naively. So instead use MITM: enumerate (
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] K0,K1) forward to the seam (2^40) is too much in
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  Python but feasible only if you reduce. 

The
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  cleanest correct approach: **MITM on the central 64-bit state.** Build a dict keyed by the se
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] am state from the forward side over K0 then refine with K1 — but since each round only
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  mixes one half, you only need to match a 32-bit half at the seam, and
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8]  each side's 32-bit value depends on a single 20-bit key. That g
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] ives two independent 2^20 sweeps plus a 32-bit hash join. Verify any sur
[tr-stream call-0028:advisor:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8] viving key quadruple against all 32 pairs, then decrypt.
